DELETE_HORIZON_FLAG_MASK = 0x40;\n    private static final byte TIMESTAMP_TYPE_MASK = 0x08;\n\n    private final ByteBuffer buffer;\n\n    DefaultRecordBatch(ByteBuffer buffer) {\n        this.buffer = buffer;\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public byte magic() {\n        return buffer.get(MAGIC_OFFSET);\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public void ensureValid() {\n        if (sizeInBytes() < RECORD_BATCH_OVERHEAD)\n            throw new CorruptRecordException(\"Record batch is corrupt (the size \" + sizeInBytes() +\n                    \" is smaller than the minimum allowed overhead \" + RECORD_BATCH_OVERHEAD + \")\");\n\n        if (!isValid())\n            throw new CorruptRecordException(\"Record is corrupt (stored crc = \" + checksum()\n                    + \", computed crc = \" + computeChecksum() + \")\");\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Gets the base timestamp of the batch which is used to calculate the record timestamps from the deltas.\n     *\n     * @return The base timestamp\n     */\n    public long baseTimestamp() {\n        return buffer.getLong(BASE_TIMESTAMP_OFFSET);\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public long maxTimestamp() {\n        return buffer.getLong(MAX_TIMESTAMP_OFFSET);\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public TimestampType timestampType() {\n        return (attributes() & TIMESTAMP_TYPE_MASK) == 0 ? TimestampType.CREATE_TIME : TimestampType.LOG_APPEND_TIME;\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public long baseOffset() {\n        return buffer.getLong(BASE_OFFSET_OFFSET);\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public long lastOffset() {\n        return baseOffset() + lastOffsetDelta();\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public long producerId() {\n        return buffer.getLong(PRODUCER_ID_OFFSET);\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public short producerEpoch() {\n        return buffer.getShort(PRODUCER_EPOCH_OFFSET);\n    }\n\n    @Override","numLines":200,"startLine":1,"totalLines":742}}}

The underlying ByteBuffer\n * is mutable, and concurrent access requires external synchronization.</p>\n *\n * <p><strong>Format:</strong> This class implements the magic v2 record batch binary format, which consists of:\n * <ul>\n *   <li>Base offset (8 bytes) - first offset in the batch</li>\n *   <li>Length (4 bytes) - size of batch data excluding the 12-byte log overhead</li>\n *   <li>Partition leader epoch (4 bytes) - assigned by broker, not included in CRC</li>\n *   <li>Magic (1 byte) - format version identifier</li>\n *   <li>CRC (4 bytes) - CRC-32C checksum of attributes through end of batch</li>\n *   <li>Attributes (2 bytes) - flags for compression, timestamp type, transactional, control, delete horizon</li>\n *   <li>Last offset delta (4 bytes) - for idempotent/transactional batches</li>\n *   <li>Producer epoch (2 bytes) - generation of the producer</li>\n *   <li>Base sequence (4 bytes) - first sequence number for duplicate detection</li>\n *   <li>Records count (4 bytes) - number of records in batch</li>\n *   <li>Records - encoded record data, optionally compressed</li>\n * </ul>\n * </p>\n *\n * <p><strong>Compaction Behavior:</strong> When records are removed during log compaction:\n * <ul>\n *   <li>Base and last offsets are preserved unchanged (from the original batch)</li>\n *   <li>Base and last sequence numbers are preserved (critical for duplicate detection)</li>\n *   <li>MaxTimestamp is preserved unless the batch becomes empty</li>\n *   <li>If all records are deleted, the batch header (overhead only) is retained temporarily\n *       to preserve producer state until the producer sends a new sequence or expires</li>\n * </ul>\n * </p>\n *\n * <p><strong>Lazy Decompression:</strong> The implementation supports lazy decompression of records via\n * {@link #streamingIterator(BufferSupplier)}, which delays decompression until records are actually\n * accessed. This significantly improves performance for small batches where buffer allocation overhead\n * dominates. The underlying ByteBuffer\n * is mutable, and concurrent access requires external synchronization.</p>\n *\n * <p><strong>Format:</strong> This class implements the magic v2 record batch binary format, which consists of:\n * <ul>\n *   <li>Base offset (8 bytes) - first offset in the batch</li>\n *   <li>Length (4 bytes) - size of batch data excluding the 12-byte log overhead</li>\n *   <li>Partition leader epoch (4 bytes) - assigned by broker, not included in CRC</li>\n *   <li>Magic (1 byte) - format version identifier</li>\n *   <li>CRC (4 bytes) - CRC-32C checksum of attributes through end of batch</li>\n *   <li>Attributes (2 bytes) - flags for compression, timestamp type, transactional, control, delete horizon</li>\n *   <li>Last offset delta (4 bytes) - number of records in batch</li>\n *   <li>Records - encoded record data, optionally compressed</li>\n * </ul>\n * </p>\n *\n * <p><strong>Compaction Behavior:</strong> When records are removed during log compaction:\n * <ul>\n *   <li>Base and last offsets are preserved unchanged (from the original batch)</li>\n *   <li>Base and last sequence numbers are preserved (critical for duplicate detection)</li>\n *   <li>MaxTimestamp is preserved unless the batch becomes empty</li>\n *   <li>If all records are deleted, the batch header (overhead only) is retained temporarily\n *       to preserve producer state until the producer sends a new sequence or expires</li>\n * </ul>\n * </p>\n *\n * <p><strong>Lazy Decompression:</strong> The implementation supports lazy decompression of records via\n * {@link #streamingIterator(BufferSupplier)}, which delays decompression until records are actually\n * accessed. This significantly improves performance for small batches where buffer allocation overhead\n * dominates. Use a {@link BufferSupplier} that reuses buffers for best performance.</p>\n *\n * <p><strong>CRC Computation:</strong> The CRC covers bytes from the attributes field to the end of the batch.\n * The partition leader epoch field is not included in the CRC to avoid recomputation when the epoch is updated\n * by the broker. DefaultRecordBatch Class Enhancement\n\n**File:** `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/record/internal/DefaultRecordBatch.java`\n\n### Class-Level Javadoc (Enhanced)\n\n**Current Status:** Has detailed class documentation (lines 45-102) with binary format specification\n\n**Enhancement:** Restructure and expand to include:\n- Thread-safety guarantee (NOT thread-safe)\n- Lazy decompression and performance characteristics\n- Compaction behavior and invariants\n- Cross-references to related classes\n\n**Suggested Replacement** (replaces lines 45-102):\n```\n/**\n * Concrete {@link RecordBatch} implementation for magic version 2 and above.\n *\n * <p><strong>Thread Safety:</strong> This class is <em>not thread-safe</em>. The underlying ByteBuffer\n * is mutable, and concurrent access requires external synchronization.</p>\n *\n * <p><strong>Format:</strong> This class implements the magic v2 record batch binary format, which consists of:\n * <ul>\n *   <li>Base offset (8 bytes) - first offset in the batch</li>\n *   <li>Length (4 bytes) - size of batch data excluding the 12-byte log overhead</li>\n *   <li>Partition leader epoch (4 bytes) - assigned by broker, not included in CRC</li>\n *   <li>Magic (1 byte) - format version identifier</li>\n *   <li>CRC (4 bytes) - CRC-32C checksum of attributes through end of batch</li>\n *   <li>Attributes (2 bytes) - flags for compression, timestamp type, transactional, control, delete horizon</li>\n *   <li>Last offset delta (4 bytes) - delta from base offset to last record offset</li>\n *   <li>Base timestamp (8 bytes) - timestamp of first record (or delete horizon if set)</li>\n *   <li>Max timestamp (8 bytes) - maximum or log-append timestamp</li>\n *   <li>Producer ID (8 bytes) - for idempotent/transactional batches</li>\n *   <li>Producer epoch (2 bytes) - generation of the producer</li>\n *   <li>Base sequence (4 bytes) - first sequence number for duplicate detection</li>\n *   <li>Records count (4 bytes) - number of records in batch</li>\n *   <li>Records - encoded record data, optionally compressed</li>\n * </ul>\n * </p>\n *\n * <p><strong>Compaction Behavior:</strong> When records are removed during log compaction:\n * <ul>\n *   <li>Base and last offsets are preserved unchanged (from the original batch)</li>\n *   <li>Base and last sequence numbers are preserved (critical for duplicate detection)</li>\n *   <li>MaxTimestamp is preserved unless the batch becomes empty</li>\n *   <li>If all records are deleted, the batch header (overhead only) is retained temporarily\n *       to preserve producer state until the producer sends a new sequence or expires</li>\n * </ul>\n * </p>\n *\n * <p><strong>Lazy Decompression:</strong> The implementation supports lazy decompression of records via\n * {@link #streamingIterator(BufferSupplier)}, which delays decompression until records are actually\n * accessed. This significantly improves performance for small batches where buffer allocation overhead\n * dominates. Use a {@link BufferSupplier} that reuses buffers for best performance.</p>\n *\n * <p><strong>CRC Computation:</strong> The CRC covers bytes from the attributes field to the end of the batch.\n * The partition leader epoch field is not included in the CRC to avoid recomputation when the epoch is updated\n * by the broker. CRC-32C (Castagnoli) polynomial is used.</p>\n *\n * @see RecordBatch\n * @see MemoryRecords\n * @see MutableRecordBatch\n */\n```\n\n### Key Public Method Additions\n\n#### baseTimestamp() - Line 166\n**Current:** Has Javadoc but could be expanded\n**Enhancement:**\n```\n/**\n * Get the base timestamp of this batch, used as the reference for record timestamp deltas.\n *\n * <p>If the delete horizon flag is set, this field contains the delete horizon timestamp rather than\n * the actual record timestamp.
